< review>
This park brings me fond memories of when I was a kid, The main feature of the park is an old aircraft that was used in Korea. It is quite different from what it was in about 1955 when I played on it, now it is completely sanitized. Back then it was all medal and glass as it came from the Air Force when retired.
The entire park is beautifully maintained and a pleasure to visit.< /review>

<rating>4</rating>< text>
Nice  clean park. Generous with the playgrounds. One can handle even the big kids and then there's one for the toddlers. There's also a splash pad for all, which interestingly is not only shaded, but has 2 benches to sit while you soak. Plenty of seating throughout, with most benches providing shade at some period during the day. There's one Gazebo only. But with shading all day, BBQ grill, and 6 picnic benches underneath, I'd say it's well equipped. An added bonus for the fitness people is the exercise machines gathered in close proximity to the playground and in direct view of the toddler playground. We'll designed layout that considers the parents who want to bur some. calories while keeping an eye on their little monkeys.<//text>

<GmapID>0x80db6176a2c8852d:0x37b065d3aadca39</GmapID>< review>
Update on my review below 2/7/2015

After I posted the review, Donnie called and said he would take care of the drain. He apologized for not getting back to me saying he had some family issues. (I won't mention them as I believe that is personal information). I told him I wasn't in a big hurry that he didn't have to make a special trip. About two weeks later he did finally make it by and fix the drain and it's working great now. I do believe Donnie is a man of integrity and is someone you can trust to do your plumbing. I have already recommended him to a family member since this was resolved.

First review,

This is a mixed review. I originally called Donnie to come out and repair a dryer vent and to fix the washing machine hookup valves that were leaking. He was also supposed to clean out all the drains in the house and tighten up all of the pumping fixtures. They came out fast and gave me a reasonable quote so I went with them after having two other services give estimates. They were there the next day to do the job. As far as I can tell the washing machine box and valves were done correctly and the dryer vent fixed properly. All of the plumbing fixtures were tightened. All was good at this point. Then next morning I used the master bath to shave and I noticed that the sink was still draining slow.  Men, you know how yucky a slow drain while shaving can get. This was a bit irritating since I just paid to have them all cleaned out. Donnie had assured me that all the sinks were draining fine, but I did not check his work at the time. Anyway, I called Donnie and left a message explaining my concern for the Master bath sink slow draining. He returned my call later that day and I explained to him my problem. He said that he would get back to me. The next day, I did not hear from him so I called and left another message to see if he would give me time when he could get back to recheck the drain. <rate>4< /rate>< Text>
First time trying this place since it's recent 'Grand Opening'.  Simple and small menu.  Prices are average for Vietnamese food.  Flavor and taste is good and on par; I wouldn't say it is exceptional.  Good enough to come back again if I need a quick bite.  My son ordered the BBQ Chicken and egg roll vermicelli.  He said the egg roll tasted okay, but did enjoy the rest of the dish.  We also ordered Thai tea, Vietnamese coffee, and an Avocado shake.  All these drinks came in a boba style cup, and tasted great.  Not super sweet, and flavor-filled.

Pro:  Free parking and plenty of it; they take most major credit cards; clean and bright inside; simple menu, drinks are great; quick service; I did hear the owner/manager speak French and Vietnamese, and English very well.

Cons:  Only one size for most items, no large; pho came with less than average steak;  very limited on the meat or beef orders; everything mainly chicken, or seafood.<//Text>

< Review>
To whom it may concern:

Find another installer.  I am a retired professional mechanical engineer.  As such, my experience includes energy and construction.  Royal‚Äôs solar energy subsidiary (Joinsolar, while its office was still located in south Chico) was contracted to install a 7.3 kw ground mounted solar system at the end of 2016.  The written contract specified (27) panels with microinverters.

Initially, a sub-contractor drilled (10) ten, eight-foot-deep anchor footings.  It was pointed out that the installation would be oriented southeast, rather than south.  The driller verified the directional error, but had to wait for the Royal representative to return.  Royal had laid out the drilling locations.  Solar generation would likely be reduced 20% and much of the lost generation ability would have to be paid at double rates (time of use) from PG&E.  The holes were re-drilled in the proper locations.  The trench was not cleared prior to utility placement.  They did route a larger than required conduit.  However, the trench and abandoned anchor holes were left for the owner to back-fill.  They left the footing caps rough with profuse quantities of spilled concrete; the expansive soil also left floating gaps of concrete islands.

The solar installation was trenched in a ninety-degree arc (i.e., no conduit fittings, straight pipe only).  The subcontractor trenched through an existing 2‚Äù waterline and 1‚Äù conduit in multiple locations.  The first waterline repair blew-out in a 25-foot-high geyser.  The 1‚Äù CPVC electric conduit was repaired with waterline fittings; I re-repaired them with the proper long-radius electrical sweep fittings.

Royal submitted an application to PG&E to connect.  The application was for a kilowatt less power than contracted.  They tell me it‚Äôs the same and PG&E just writes it differently.  No, peak power is peak power.  Final payment is withheld.  Royal pulled the (27) 215watt Siemen‚Äôs inverters and install (28) 250watt Enphase inverters; they also added a 28th solar panel.  The system now has a peak output of 7 kw.  I can live with that.

A summer or two ago a swampy area, with standing surface water, appeared in the back field. Unlike metal pipe, PVC does not corrode underground.  Buried PVC should stay intact for hundreds of years.  Properly installed solvent welded joints should last just as long as the pipe substrate.  I was not looking forward to the repair of an item that should never need repair.  It was the final straw and was the reason for this review.  A couple of man-days were wasted fixing something that should never need fixing‚Ä¶if it had been done right originally.

First, dig down in the swamp to find the leaking pipeline.  Next, determine the leak location.  The pipeline must be followed until the failure point is found.  Wet clay soil does not readily release from digging tools; the blades must be scrapped.  Fun.  Dig until the suspected leaking fitting is exposed.  Recharge the water line.  Water and air begin discharging, thus confirming the leak location.  Shut-off the water again.

The hole is enlarged to provide access to the failed joint.  A 1‚Äù conduit lies atop the failure point.  A 6-foot section of the conduit must be removed to gain access to the failed pipe below.  Soil is excavated from below the offending pipeline as well.  While digging around the pipe, one of the joints appears to shift.  Lifting the pipe causes the joint to separate intact.  Prying on the other end gets the other end to release as well.  Each pipe end was inserted about ¬Ω‚Äù (less than 40%) into the fitting.  Properly glued joints fuse so well that ¬º‚Äù radial fitting sections are difficult to separate from the pipe with a hammer and sharp-edged chisel‚Ä¶. impossible if the outside fitting perimeter is intact.  Solvent welded joints also don‚Äôt degrade with time.  It‚Äôs a homogeneous material.  Both water and conduit lines were repaired and tested.  No leaks were detected.  All new joints have better than 80% insertion and were not glued in muddy water.

Sincerely,

Greg Shea, PE
CA License M025117< /Review>

I am not a customer of Royal Aire and have nothing negative to say about their services. However, I do have a problem with their door to door solicitation. <user_id>112983254715416302555< /user_id><user_name>Robert Sockey</user_name><date>1379538425159< /date>< rate>

< Text>
I was out of town when my wife called on a hot Sunday afternoon and explained that the air conditioning stopped working.  I asked if the fan on the outdoor unit was running and she said it was not and that it was making a humming noise.  I suggested she call someone she could trust to look at it.  She called Royal Aire and within an hour the technician arrived.  He found that the motor start capacitor was defective and replaced it with a after market (not original equipment) capacitor.  The unit began working immediately and the work was completed in less than an hour.  The bill was $390.00.  The capacitor cost $251.00 dollars and the remainder was for the service call and labor.  He said he could sell her a maintenance agreement for only $20.00 more.  The maintenance agreement provides for two additional future service calls to check to see if the unit is operating correctly and, if parts are required, it provides a 15% discount on the parts.  My wife thought it was a good deal and signed for the maintenance agreement.  The total cost was $410.00.

I am an electrical engineer.  I know what a motor start capacitor is and its function.  I also know a motor start capacitor costs anywhere from $20 to $$90 depending on the type required.  the original equipment capacitor for our unit costs about $40.  The aftermarket capacitor that the technician installed was an Amrad Engineering Turbo 200X.  It sells on line for $60 to $100 depending on where you buy it.  Another company in Chico told me they would have charged me $30 to $60 for the part depending on the specific type.

It is my opinion that Royal Aire overcharged my wife for the part.  My wife doesn't know a motor start capacitor from a cement mixer.  I think he took advantage of her.  He could have told her the part cost $500 and she would have paid it.  If I had been there I would have paid for the technician's time and replaced the capacitor myself if he refused to give me a fair price for the part.  I wouldn't have signed up for the maintenance agreement.  I called and emailed the owner of Royal Aire and asked him to call me.  He never did.< /Text>

I've been doing business with Royal Aire for approximately 6 years now and have spent well in excess of $10,000 with them. They've been 5 star great. Until now. So when my wife called me, while I was at work, to say the AC wasn't working, it was 108* outside and 90* inside, I told her to stay calm and carry on while I immediately called Royal Aire. It was 4:39 PM and I was pleasantly surprised to find out they'd come out, after hours, on a holiday, for only $30 extra, and they'd see me between 8-10. Sweet. Upon my arrival at home I found a hot and sweaty family melting around the house. I immediately set out to troubleshoot the problem myself and eliminated several things. At this time a friendly and neat Royal Aire employee showed up (on time) and I filled him in on what I had done. He scratched his head, perplexed, and said he'd need to call in the multi zone expert (he was only qualified to work on equipment). I walked him through how the zones worked and explained how to troubleshoot them. Once I confirmed they weren't the problem we checked several other areas, at my suggestion, and ultimately discovered the problem, a frozen over coil. The solution: let it thaw out and carry on. Done. After 20 minutes of following me around, I was surprised when the fellow charged me full price for the pleasure of showing him how to do his job. Don't get me wrong, I'm positive he'd have figured it out in due time (after calling in a zone expert).

I called the next day and spoke to "Bob" the service manager. Bob tried convincing me he'd already lost money by only charging me full price. I explained to him his price structure was his own problem and even if he lost money on me he had more than been compensated over the years by the business and dollars I already gave the company. Bob then tried to up-sell me on a service plan (no thanks, I can hose off my filters and unit myself, thanks). Ultimately we agreed on a price where I didn't feel cheated and Royal Aire was more than compensated for their drive and tour of my home. I didn't charge them for the impromptu training I gave their employee.

The problem was Bob's terrible attitude even after our negotiated settlement. Never a "sorry," "our apologies" or "we understand." No, nothing from Bob but animosity and confrontation. You already have $10,000 of service from me and countless more dollars of profit if our relationship continues in the future. Your 3 star rating will go up if your attitude improves. It will also go down if my refund check never appears. I'm watching you Bob.

Edit: Well, Bob followed through with his promise on our settled agreement. Kudos to you Bob. Will I continue my service with Royal Aire? Yes, however, they're on probation. I've upped their star ratting but I'm holding back on the 5th star for now. The next time I do business with them, if they give me the fantastic service I'm used to, they'll earn back the star.

Bottom line: Royal Aire is a trusted and true company but needs to polish up their custom service in regards to complaints.<//Text>

< Text>
I ordered few staple dishes so i can fairly compare to other local Thai places. I liked the service, there was no wait. I ordered shrimp basil fried rice, chicken pad thai, bbq pork and yellow chicken curry. The basil rice was delicious with a kick. The curry and pad thai were also very good. The bbq pork did not have the grilled flavor i was looking for, it was thick cut, and looked like it was cooked by boiling with some grilled marks. It was very pale and it was in the dry side. I loved the smaller lunch portions - the whole thing with a beer was $54, pretty good. I would go there again<//Text>

< Text>
So on this day my dad and his girlfriend picked me up for a early dinner. The other Thai restaurant a few blocks down was closed so we decided to check out Orchids. I am pleased to announce that we made a wonderful and delicious choice. The atmosphere inside Orchids was clean and very spacious. Staff was kind and welcoming. There was only a couple of other tables with diners and we were seated in a nice cozy corner table right near the kitchen. It was past 3pm when the lunch special ends but the staff was kind enough to let us choose from the lunch menu nonetheless. We began with some refreshing ice cold water as we went through the menu to select our items. We ordered A green sesame ginger salad that was bursting with fresh delicious flavors and not overpowering at all. I even used the dressing to pour over my jasmine rice which had some hints of lemongrass and cilantro that added so nicely to the rice. We followed up with a order of the Tom Kha coconut soup with chicken. Very fresh and delicious flavors. For our main entree we ordered the hot chili green beans dish with chicken. It had lemongrass, young bell peppers bell peppers, bamboo shoots, and lemongrass. Everything went so well with each other and we had a very pleasant dining experience. The Thai Ice Tea was also on point.
Orchids Thai restaurant is definitely a place i will be dining at again with friends family and even a date. Thank you Orchids for a wonderful and pleasant authentic Thai dining experience. See you soon. Next time ill try the curries, bbq, and noodle dishes. üòä< /Text>

< Review>
I had a negative experience here in 2019, after a positive experience in 2016-2017. In the midst of a household move, I temporarily need storage for about a third of a garage worth of stuff. Based on a positive experience I had renting at this Extra Space location in 2016/2017, I figured it'd be easy and worthwhile to come back here this time around. Unfortunately, I encountered barrier after barrier. On Monday the 22nd of July 2019, I stopped by twice (during posted business hours) only to find the office closed+locked, with nobody there. On Tuesday I stopped by again, and happily discovered the office open and staffed. First, they acted like my request for a no-elevator/no-stairs 8x10 unit was surprising. (Why? I have no idea.) Then, they were dismayed that I was happy to rent the unit sight unseen, based on my past experience at this location. They insisted they couldn't possibly rent me an empty storage room without first showing it to me, "just in case", because after all "you'd never buy a car without test-driving it". (They were shocked when I explained that I had in fact bought my car online, sight unseen, with great results.) Then, they seemed annoyed when I didn't need more than 5 seconds to examine the empty storage room to confirm that yes in fact I do want to rent it. Finally, they insisted that I must have insurance to cover my stuff (why?) and, when I explained yes I do have insurance and the policy number, they insisted that I must have a full copy of the policy on hand in order to proceed. At this point I decided that they just weren't interested in renting to me, for whatever reason, and so I took my business elsewhere.</Review>

<Name>Chip Chapin</Name>< Review>
Very good management, keeps things clean and well run.  Prices seem competitive, but it is still expensive. However unlike some storage places, there is nobody on-site except during office hours. Some storage places alarm the individual units and key the alarm to the entry of the corresponding gate code. Not here.  So units are vulnerable to anyone with 60 seconds and a portable angle grinder, especially the outside units.  Another problem with the outside units: when they blow off the driveway a lot of dirt goes under the door into your unit.  I've had three separate units here and they all had that problem.  I still like this place, it's very convenient and the staff is excellent.  But I've seen better.<//Review>
